    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="review_170312578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170312578" />
    <a title="Ruth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846788-ruth"><img alt="Ruth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535825273p2/3846788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170312578?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruth" href="/user/show/3846788-ruth">Ruth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170312578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4360454308734992495">I nearly melted when Conrad was introduced. That strong, silent, protective guy, why, he was even sexier than Edward Cullen! And although he didn't sparkle, he certainly made up for it by his sorrowful brooding, which my heart soared out to. I mean, who DOESN'T understand when someone who is in pain turns to drinking and picking fights at parties?There is just something so alluring, so captivating, about Conrad, because what he does not say or do in words is immediately engraved in my ever-lovin</span>
  <span id="freeText4360454308734992495" style="display:none">I nearly melted when Conrad was introduced. That strong, silent, protective guy, why, he was even sexier than Edward Cullen! And although he didn't sparkle, he certainly made up for it by his sorrowful brooding, which my heart soared out to. I mean, who DOESN'T understand when someone who is in pain turns to drinking and picking fights at parties?There is just something so alluring, so captivating, about Conrad, because what he does not say or do in words is immediately engraved in my ever-loving heart. I totally, completely, 101% understand why Belly loved him her entire life. <br /><br />As for Belly, heavy burdens are hard to accept, but World War 3.5 broke out the Summer She Turned Pretty. I totally sympathized with her, with all those choices she had to make. As a famous poet once wrote, "Two roads diverged into a yellow wood. And I, I took the one less traveled by." Like this, Belly did just that. Instead of romancing just one guy, she made the unusual, yet incredibly understandable choice to romance THREE GUYS. And WOW! Was this beautifully conflicting love SQUARE intense!! nearly had a heart-attack, my heart beat so loud in my ears, when THIS scene happened:<br /><br />"Get out of my face," Conrad growled.<br /><br />"No." Jeremiah stepped closer, until their faces were inches apart, just like ours had been not fifteen minutes before. <br /><br />In a dangerous voice, Conrad said, "I'm warning you, Jeremiah."<br /><br />So well spoken, so unique, so original, AMEN BROTHER. No scene has truly ever frightened me so much, to the point where I just had to wrench this book out of my own hands and go take ten minutes' breather in the bathroom. But since this review isn't marked with SPOILER, I'll just say that you will have to stop and re-read a few times what has actually happened at this 90-degree-climax. <br /><br />I sympathize so well with Belly, and again, I praise Jenny Han for relating SO WELL, SO WELL, I SAY, to teen girls. Ms. Han really brought this scene to life, it was so intense and completely, reasonably dramatic, my heart literally skipped a beat and I almost had an asthma attack:<br /><br />"I stood by the fire alone and pretended to warm my hands even though they weren't cold. That's when I saw him. He was standing alone too, drinking a bottle of water. It didn't seem like he knew anybody either, since he was standing all by himself." Ah! Ms. Han, you have such an elegant, easy way of making contradicting words and plain sentences flow so naturally! So barely noticeable! Continuing on, <br /> <br />He looked like he was my age. But there was something about him that seemed safe and comfortable, like he was younger than me even though he wasn't." Again, what is this? A beautiful paradox? No, paradox isn't even the word. I was so dumbfoundedly awestruck by this sentence that I had to stop, pause, and wonder, what was going to happen next? Really, at this point in the book, things really take a turn around the bend.<br /><br />BUT. I am truly amazed by the way Jenny Han has a talent with words, and finally releasing reader's from their growing suspicion that something more was going on between Belly, Jeremiah, and Conrad:<br /><br />"Things had been weird with me and Conrad and also with me and Jeremiah-an impossible thought crept its way into my head. Was it possible they didn't want me with Came? Because THEY, like, had feelings for me?" I love how Jenny Han seems to remember how teenagers act, because by putting that single unnecessary "like" into the sentence truly, legit, won me over. I had no idea how poetic daily teen slang could have been. <br /><br />There are some things I absolutely ADORED about Belly. She was so realistic in the sense that I felt she was RIGHT IN MY HEAD. Like, seriously, like honestly, like LEGIT:<br /><br />"I didn't answer his question. Instead I said, "I was really good! I could have been dancing in a company by now!" I couldn't have. I wasn't that good, not by any stretch of the imagination." You can tell by this simply put declaration that Belly has given, how much she wants this guy to love her. She has gone so far, and given away her dignity, to BOAST HOW GOOD SHE IS AT BALLET. <br /><br />""Maybe we can come back later." I knew he didn't mean it. Part of me was mad, and part of me was relieved. It was like craving a fried peanut butter and banana sandwich and then realizing two bites in that you didn't want it after all. I snatched my sweatshirt from him and said, "Don't do me any favors, Cam." Then I walked away as fast as I could, and sand kicked up behind me. I thought he might follow me, but he didn't." <br /><br />This realistic intervention, this sudden, quirky, show of personality really is truly realistic. After all, EVERY teen needs to have their mood swings, but yet, this has shown Belly's true, twisting feelings for the guy she is talking to. I am truly amazed, I had no idea authors could get into my head so easily.<br /><br />I feel proud to be a whiny, annoying teenager, because by the ways things turned out in the end of THE SUMMER I TURNED PRETTY, there is no doubt that I will Someday Find My Prince in the two hot guys I've obviously known all my life, but who started expressing their feelings towards me the Summer I Turned Pretty.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4360454308734992495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_98918242" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98918242" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98918242?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98918242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1058514469476526313">There was so much about this book that bothered me, and I almost gave up on it several times. I think the thing that bothered me most though was the protagonist. Very often, if I can't connect or feel compassion for the main character, the book has slim to no chance of winning me over. In my opinion, Belly was such an immature, self-focused and petulant child. Her actions and feelings about events and people really were annoying that I wanted to shake some sense into her, I'll provide more speci</span>
  <span id="freeText1058514469476526313" style="display:none">There was so much about this book that bothered me, and I almost gave up on it several times. I think the thing that bothered me most though was the protagonist. Very often, if I can't connect or feel compassion for the main character, the book has slim to no chance of winning me over. In my opinion, Belly was such an immature, self-focused and petulant child. Her actions and feelings about events and people really were annoying that I wanted to shake some sense into her, I'll provide more specifics in a few. <br /><br />But first, one of the biggest things that irk me, and for those that know my reading style, they will laugh because I've said this often times before, I can't stand when an author doesn't tell you the name of the person narrating the story or who the story is about. Very few, maybe like one or two books (The Gargoyle being one) have been exempt from this number one rule of mine, <i> I want to know who is talking to me or who the story is about right away!</i> "Belly" doesn't cut it , especially when I find belly buttons gross and cringe-worthy. Ewwww! It's not until more than half way through the book that we find out her real name is Isabel, but by then it was too late, I was calling her Bellatrix in my head and couldn't get it out. Sorry, but it just happened naturally.<br /><br />Overall, it bothered me how selfish Bellatrix… errr… I mean Belly was to those in her life, including family and friends. For example, her father tried so hard with her by buying her books, a piano and fixing up a room in his new apartment in the hopes she'd come to enjoy spending some time with him, but NOOOOO she didn't like the books he chose, the piano was out of tune and she wanted the yellow sheets, not the pink scratchy sheets. Ugh! Also, she has no real heartfelt relationships with ANYONE. She uses her best friend Taylor by inviting her to the beach house for the sole purpose that maybe she'll be able to fit in better with the crowd because of Taylor, but it ends up backfiring so she ends up resenting her BF. Her relationship with her brother is downright mean and shallow, nothing heartfelt or aww-worthy there. Even her friendship with Jeremiah and Conrad left much to be desired. It bothered me when Jeremiah and Belly overheard a convo between their mothers about Suzanne's breast cancer and Belly had no clue how to comfort him, all she could think of saying was <i>"I hope your mom doesn't lose a boob." </i> Really? That's all you got?? Glad you kept that in your little air-filled noggin and didn't say it out loud. How about just give him a hug and ask him if he's okay or wants to talk?? There were so many opportunities for her to show some depth and growth, but she just fell flat IMO.<br /><br />BUT, the thing that bothered me the most is that she crushes on two brothers. That's just gross!! Pick one and stop with the <i>"I like Jeremiah... no... I like Conrad... oh I shared a Twizzler with Jeremiah now I like him more again... Oh wait I like Conrad's dark and brooding side, I change my mind, I like him better."</i> That gets irritating right quick next to her feeling that life got better for her when she turned pretty. No really, she felt <i> I'm pretty now, life is like sooooo good now! I love being sooooo pretty. I was ugly before and an outsider, but now I'm pretty. Yay for me!</i> Whatevs! *shakes head*<br /><br />Lastly, the writing was simple and the storyline wasn't very complex at all, except for trying to figure out who this Belly girl really was. The story did switch back from present to past in random ways, but I don't consider that complex, just slightly irksome. The one thing the book did have going for it was the setting. I like seaside, beachfront, boardwalk settings, but that wasn't enough to hook me… I'd much prefer a Dessen book to provide me that fix. All in all, there's better out there IMHO.<br /><br />Okay, this review feels sloppy and random... I'll just blame it on the book. DONE! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1058514469476526313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15707594110286879357" style="display:none">I didn't like this book.<br /><br />The thing that bother me the most was the girl, Belly, she was VERY annoying. I also just couldn't connect with the story, I mean all the book is about how much she loooooves Conrad (one of her mom's best friend's sons) and everything in her lifes revolves around Conrad.<br /><br />It was bording on obsession actually, she came across as pathetic. <div id="review_182264000" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182264000" />
    <a title=" Arushi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5620615-arushi"><img alt=" Arushi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337664395p2/5620615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182264000?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182264000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4833266372380718278">This book made me want to cry tears of <b>blood</b>.<br/><br/>Belly, if someone is hurting and tells you to stop talking, you don’t just kiss them. Also, if you and your friend overhear about his mother’s breast cancer, you don’t think thoughts like <i>‘oh, I hope she doesn’t loose a boob’</i><br/><br/>No. Just, no.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380352645ra/706049.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>My husband does not approve of you.<br/><br/><b>Low Points in this book:</b><br/><i>
  <u>Belly.</u>
</i>Girl, this is for being whiny and obnoxious. Also, for being a bitch to your mother and thinking that she would never ever do anything for you and f</span>
  <span id="freeText4833266372380718278" style="display:none">This book made me want to cry tears of <b>blood</b>.<br><br>Belly, if someone is hurting and tells you to stop talking, you don’t just kiss them. Also, if you and your friend overhear about his mother’s breast cancer, you don’t think thoughts like <i>‘oh, I hope she doesn’t loose a boob’</i><br><br>No. Just, no.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380352645ra/706049.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>My husband does not approve of you.<br><br><b>Low Points in this book:</b><br><i>
  <u>Belly.</u>
</i>Girl, this is for being whiny and obnoxious. Also, for being a bitch to your mother and thinking that she would never ever do anything for you and for not appreciating her at all. For confusing me every two seconds by saying <i>“i dunt even lyk Conrad. I lyk Jere. And Cam. but omg, hes sexeh mmm” </i><br><i>
  <u>Conrad.</u>
</i>Are you sure you’re going to college next year boy? My eight year old cousin is more mature than you. Don't you worry though, puberty will hit you soon enough.<br><i>
  <u>Cam.</u>
</i><s>I liked you. How could you do this to me?</s> That is for letting Belly <b>use</b> you to make Conrad jealous. If you hadn’t called her those two times at the end, I would have saved you some of my respect but nope. Sorry.<br><br><b>High points in this book:</b><br><i>
  <u>Jeremiah.</u>
</i>Since Cam is out of the picture, you’re obviously going to magically turn evil and fuck shit up and hurt Belly so she can hate you and have babies with Conrad. Even though you’ve been her rock and best friend and remembered her birthday. You will feel like shit when the series ends for sticking up for her but guess what? Tough fucking luck.<br><br><i>
  <u>Taylor.</u>
</i>You got slut shamed for kissing Belly’s brother and made her flip shit. You're invited to party with me.<br><br>That’s it. <br><br>Call me a masochist but I’ll read the next two books. Why? Because I like to torture myself that’s why. Or maybe because I’m hoping that Belly grows up and kicks Conrad once between the legs. My life will be complete.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/219406176?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judith (Judith&#39;sChoiceReads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judith (Judith&#39;sChoiceReads)" href="/user/show/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads">Judith (Judith&#39;sChoiceReads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=books-i-want-to-own">books-i-want-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=crazy-phenomenal">crazy-phenomenal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=crazy-romantic">crazy-romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=series-i-love">series-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=hunks-of-the-world">hunks-of-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=must-haves">must-haves</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=heroines-with-spunk">heroines-with-spunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219406176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9162322054048137250"><b>Rating:</b> 4 1/2 stars <br/><br/><b>Characters:</b> 5 stars <br/><br/><b>Setting:</b> 5 stars<br/><br/><b>Plot:</b> 4 <br/><br/><b> Honourable Mention:</b> To Susannah. For being the embodiment of summer, and pretty much perfect. <br/><br/><b> ***OOH, <i>possible</i> spoilers ahead guys, watch out!</b><br/><br/>Well. So that was...<br/><br/><a href='http://s1114.photobucket.com/albums/k525/judy10001/?action=view&current=tumblr_lisoz4zh0z1qb8zso.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360656ra/711541.gif' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I feel a lot like this: <br/><br/><a href='http://s1114.photobucket.com/albums/k525/judy10001/?action=view&current=tumblr_la7be0de1E1qbngwl.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360656ra/711542.gif' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Because I am sure of two things: <br/><br/>1.) I freaking love this series. And <b>Conrad.</b> I really freaking adore him, more than Jeremiah I am happy to say. Ah, to be young and fictionally in love...<br/><br/>2.) This is my new favourite series. <br/><br/><s>And three, becau</s></span>
  <span id="freeText9162322054048137250" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> 4 1/2 stars <br><br><b>Characters:</b> 5 stars <br><br><b>Setting:</b> 5 stars<br><br><b>Plot:</b> 4 <br><br><b> Honourable Mention:</b> To Susannah. For being the embodiment of summer, and pretty much perfect. <br><br><b> ***OOH, <i>possible</i> spoilers ahead guys, watch out!</b><br><br>Well. So that was...<br><br><a href="http://s1114.photobucket.com/albums/k525/judy10001/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_lisoz4zh0z1qb8zso.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360656ra/711541.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I feel a lot like this: <br><br><a href="http://s1114.photobucket.com/albums/k525/judy10001/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_la7be0de1E1qbngwl.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360656ra/711542.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Because I am sure of two things: <br><br>1.) I freaking love this series. And <b>Conrad.</b> I really freaking adore him, more than Jeremiah I am happy to say. Ah, to be young and fictionally in love...<br><br>2.) This is my new favourite series. <br><br><s>And three, because I'm just boss that way:</s><br><br>3.) Reading this series takes my mind away from the horror that is snow all around, and while I'm reading this all I imagine are rainbows, the ocean and glorious warmth. Basically by endeavouring to read the rest of the series, I'd like to delude myself longer. <br><br><br><b>What I'm getting at here:</b> <br><br>Is that this is a well-rounded and great book. I was so hesitant to try it because the other beachy novel on my CR shelf is stale and quite frankly, irrelevant to me at the moment. This however, this was relevant! It had so much heart and such soul...I love Belly, and Beck's boys. <br><br>You know at the back of books where the book blurb is all like, "...A true tale of touching inspiration and growth?" Well I feel <i>just</i> like that! I feel like donning my creep glasses and jacket and writing something inspirational too! You know what! I will:<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/creep" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360656ra/711543.gif" alt="creep Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>One step at a time, my friends, this book has touched me. Severely. <br><br><b>Summary (brief):</b> Belly is this awkward teenager I couldn't help relating to because at her age I was just as clueless, if not more! She turns pretty one summer and everything changes, her two life-long "friends" begin to act differently and tensions rise as further complications threaten to ruin the tradition of Summer. Let me start off by saying Cousin's beach is a place I most definitely have to go!<br><br>I started off reading this with a bit of a raised brow because I didn't know if the importance Belly and everyone held for this place would rub off unto me or not. I knew that I really wanted it to and am all kinds of crazy mad-glad it did. Some authors can try to capture the <i>idea</i> of summer, but what Han actually does is that she grabs a hold of the very definition, transforms it and personifies it into a person. And one. <br><br>Both Belly and Susannah were summer personified to me; summer at different stages. Belly is at the beginning, like a beach inexperienced or sand yet to be tread--she's smooth canvas. Susannah on the other hand is the shore at twilight and she symbolizes something we have yet to ever see, the <i>end</i> of summer. She doesn't get there in this book but the gradual decline taking place is made very evident, and yet through it all she's this picture of dignity, something to behold. I kind of love this woman. <br><br><i>Women</i> if you factor in Belly and Han, the author, because I adore them too. This book was so good that I left thinking I would nick-name my baby Belly somehow. <br><br><br><a href="http://s1114.photobucket.com/albums/k525/judy10001/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_lbka7mRx5s1qaj5jro1_500.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360656ra/711544.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Yeah, I know!</b><br><br>It was just this awesome ride and reading it was such a privilege, I cannot begin to explain. I have nowhere to begin because I am at a loss for words, all I can say is that I have been thoroughly pleased. And for once (those of you who know me will know just how much of a breach from character this is) I cannot focus solely on the men, I just can't It would be an insult to do so, because despite the fact that they were major and wonderful parts of this book, <i>they</i> just didn't seem to matter more than the overall story. <br><br>What mattered were Susannah and Belly and their growth because there was so much happening here. So much character development took place that it was crazy and incredible at the same time! This feeling of watching someone learn and transform into something better than what they once were is what drives me to read, I hardly see enough of it in real life. <br><br>There were things I wished were better resolved, say Cam and Mr. Fisher, I wanted to know the reason for the impending divorce, and I also thought the adorable geek that is Cam deserved at least an explanation! No fair, Bells. <br><br>Other than that I am good. So good that I already have the second book sitting around somewhere waiting. I'll try reading a bit of <u>Endless Summer</u> again but if nothing comes of it, I'm dropping it like a hot potato. <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/hot%20potato" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360656ra/711545.gif" alt="chowder hot potato Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Because every book should be as good as this one.</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9162322054048137250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1855013391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1855013391" />
    <a title="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63164992-grace-burtsbooks"><img alt="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517623708p2/63164992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1855013391?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" href="/user/show/63164992-grace-burtsbooks">Grace (BURTSBOOKS)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63164992-grace-burtsbooks?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63164992-grace-burtsbooks?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1855013391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7450950765361376128">Hi, so this book isn't technically a five-star read. It's a little cliche and a lot cheesy and centres around a love triangle and just is not a literary masterpiece. I don't care about any of that though because this is the book I was reading before I was a reader. This is the book that made me want to read. This was the first book I read into the night. The first book I couldn't put down. This was the book of my preteen years and the nostalgia I feel for this book surpasses any reservations I h</span>
  <span id="freeText7450950765361376128" style="display:none">Hi, so this book isn't technically a five-star read. It's a little cliche and a lot cheesy and centres around a love triangle and just is not a literary masterpiece. I don't care about any of that though because this is the book I was reading before I was a reader. This is the book that made me want to read. This was the first book I read into the night. The first book I couldn't put down. This was the book of my preteen years and the nostalgia I feel for this book surpasses any reservations I have about the plot now that I'm not 12 anymore. I've read this book upwards of fifteen times and no matter what stage of my life I'm at, I love it. These characters feel like family. The beach house feels like my own vacation home and the words feel like they live in my brain. So yeah, it isn't a perfect book and is the exact opposite of what I tend to lean towards nowadays but forever and ever and ever it will be a symbol of my love of reading and I will always be fond.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7450950765361376128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1648619410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648619410" />
    <a title="Nina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44463467-nina"><img alt="Nina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597502267p2/44463467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1648619410?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina" href="/user/show/44463467-nina">Nina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7956260-the-summer-i-turned-pretty">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44463467-nina?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648619410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5537027545340554065"><b>*** 2.5 stars ***</b><br/><br/><i>“Would you rather live one perfect day over and over or live your life with no perfect days but just decent ones?” </i><br/><br/>I started reading ‘The Summer I Turned Pretty’ because I felt like a reading slump was heading my way and a couple of people told me that this would be the perfect book to read in such a situation. And it actually is because this was such a quick read and I finished it in less than a day. It’s also a perfect summer read that you can enjoy while spending your time on</span>
  <span id="freeText5537027545340554065" style="display:none"><b>*** 2.5 stars ***</b><br /><br /><i>“Would you rather live one perfect day over and over or live your life with no perfect days but just decent ones?” </i><br /><br />I started reading ‘The Summer I Turned Pretty’ because I felt like a reading slump was heading my way and a couple of people told me that this would be the perfect book to read in such a situation. And it actually is because this was such a quick read and I finished it in less than a day. It’s also a perfect summer read that you can enjoy while spending your time on the beach.<br /><br />But even though it was a cute book, it was also very cliché and often quite predictable. But that wasn’t the worst thing about this book because it’s something I can usually live with. The worst thing was definitely the main character, Belly. She was such an annoying character and such a whiny little brat. I know that this is a coming of age novel and many girls that age might tend to behave like her but in my opinion, she was just way over to the top. She was complaining so much, she literally made me want to rip my hair out at some points. <br /><br />Belly was constantly going on about how badly the boys were treating her, how they were always treating her like a child (though she was the one that constantly acted like a 9-year-old) and how they never asked her to come along when going somewhere. She literally made them responsible for everything she didn’t like, for example how she didn’t know anyone in the town they spend their summer breaks in because it would’ve been their job to take her to parties … like seriously though, what the hell? She can walk and talk, she should’ve left the house herself and made her own friends in that town instead of spending all her summer sulking because the three boys just preferred doing their own things. <br /><br />She was literally such a pain in the neck, I think she was even more annoying than America from the Selection series and I actually thought that was impossible.<br /><br />All of this just made me feel like I was way too old for this book and I really don’t know if I’ll actually continue this series even though I liked the other characters. I loved Conrad, Jeremiah and Steven and I also think that this book was generally very well written. But because of the main character and the fact that I felt a little too old for the entire story, I can only give TSITP 2.5 out of 5 stars.<br /><br />(PS: I’m sorry about the fact that half of this review is just me complaining about the MC but she was literally driving me insane!)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5537027545340554065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2296250095" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2296250095" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2296250095?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416968290" href="/book/show/6584189-the-summer-i-turned-pretty">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2296250095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15688264100969742714"><br/>I read it in one sitting. Even though there’s a thin air of sadness coating the story’s atmosphere, to me it was still familiar, warm and comforting. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/151371.Jenny_Han' title='Jenny Han' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Han’s</a> writing and stories usually do that. I appreciate how the first book to this trilogy is more like a coming off age novel more than anything. The writing actually reminds me of that of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/259068.Shug' title='Shug by Jenny Han' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shug</a>, a middle school book written by Ms. Han which was completely endearing. <br/><br/>The entire story happens in a span of an entire summer but I was impressed w</span>
  <span id="freeText15688264100969742714" style="display:none"><br />I read it in one sitting. Even though there’s a thin air of sadness coating the story’s atmosphere, to me it was still familiar, warm and comforting. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/151371.Jenny_Han" title="Jenny Han" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Han’s</a> writing and stories usually do that. I appreciate how the first book to this trilogy is more like a coming off age novel more than anything. The writing actually reminds me of that of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/259068.Shug" title="Shug by Jenny Han" rel="nofollow noopener">Shug</a>, a middle school book written by Ms. Han which was completely endearing. <br /><br />The entire story happens in a span of an entire summer but I was impressed with how the book managed to get me to know the individual characters in the story so well and in only a matter of less than 300 pages. The tangle of young love and love triangles expected of childhood friendships is adorably portrayed. I can’t wait to read the second book which I’m doing exactly now. One of the perks of getting sick- I get to stay at home and read all day long. Woot! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15688264100969742714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jessie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6949365-jessie"><img alt="Jessie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372869884p2/6949365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307469080?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6949365-jessie?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6949365-jessie?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6949365-jessie?shelf=annoying-main-character">annoying-main-character</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6949365-jessie?shelf=couldnt-stop-reading">couldnt-stop-reading</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307469080" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer344753266488863973">Just some thoughts.<br/><br/>Actual rating: 2.5 stars<br/><br/><u>
  <b>Belly:</b>
</u> <br/>Belly's pretty much clueless the whole time. She thinks the world revolves around her but it doesn't. She's shallow as hell. But for some reason, she doesn't annoy me too much. (She was getting on my nerves a lot toward the end of the book, though.) Overall, she's just an okay character.<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Though I can't believe how she treated Cam...she just abandoned him after using him for so long. What the heck?  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I also don't g</span>
  <span id="freeText344753266488863973" style="display:none">Just some thoughts.<br /><br />Actual rating: 2.5 stars<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Belly:</b>
</u> <br />Belly's pretty much clueless the whole time. She thinks the world revolves around her but it doesn't. She's shallow as hell. But for some reason, she doesn't annoy me too much. (She was getting on my nerves a lot toward the end of the book, though.) Overall, she's just an okay character.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Though I can't believe how she treated Cam...she just abandoned him after using him for so long. What the heck?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I also don't get how she could be best friends with Taylor. She's such an ass. And the mother-daughter relationship? Ugh. Please, just grow up, Belly. And stop pining over Conrad all the time. There are things in life that are much more important than boys. Just...please start using your brain. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Conrad:</b>
</u> <br />Conrad's pretty much selfish the whole time. I didn't like how he was all mean to Belly and everyone around him. Even though bad stuff kept happening and all, it's not right to take it out on others. I still root for Conrad, though. &lt;3 (I love the name, by the way!)<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Jeremiah: </b>
</u><br />Sweet, funny, cute. The pole opposite of Conrad. Although he's a bit lacking of personality and depth, he's a pretty decent character.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Steven:</b>
</u><br />I actually liked him. Even though he's not an important character, I like how realistic he is. Although I didn't like how he never includes Belly in their little team and all, I suppose that's how a brother should act in real life.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Cam:</b>
</u><br />It really surprised me how *important* he is in this book. I thought he was going to be <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[abandoned <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> a lot sooner, so it really shocked me how he was around so much and stayed toward the end. I still feel bad for him, though. He was a pretty nice guy.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>The plot: </b>
</u><br />Basically nothing happens. I was expecting something...between <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Conrad and Belly. But it doesn't happen until the very end. *sigh* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The story was a bit...flat. It's like reading about what Belly's schedule over and over again, which means swimming, movie, Cam, more Cam, pining, drooling over Conrad. I just...couldn't care less.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>The writing: </b>
</u><br />I do NOT appreciate the weird constant switch of time period. It's both confusing and frustrating as hell. One minute you're reading what is happening right now, and the other it just suddenly jumps to something that happened that morning or even years ago. It's really annoying. So, please, stop that.<br /><br /><u>
  <b> The ending: </b>
</u><br />What is with that ending? I don't get it. It's just so random. I'm confused here.<br /><br />Despite all that, I did like it, it was a quick and entertaining read. It might be a bit boring at times, but it's still pretty fun most of the time. <br /><br />This is basically your average summer read. Nothing special, but entertaining nonetheless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="344753266488863973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415677371p2/36817401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2478949380?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10101548-the-summer-i-turned-pretty">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2478949380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17844224030136554525">The Summer I Turned Pretty by Jenny Han is the first book in the young adult contemporary Summer series. The story is a bit of a coming of age tale with a side of romance and family dynamics.<br/><br/>Fifteen, almost sixteen, Isabelle or Belly as she’s always been known is ready for yet another summer at the beach. Each year Belly’s mother packs up Belly and her brother and heads to her best friend’s beach house with Susannah and her two sons, Conrad and Jeremiah, at Cousins Beach.<br/><br/>Every year Belly has got</span>
  <span id="freeText17844224030136554525" style="display:none">The Summer I Turned Pretty by Jenny Han is the first book in the young adult contemporary Summer series. The story is a bit of a coming of age tale with a side of romance and family dynamics.<br /><br />Fifteen, almost sixteen, Isabelle or Belly as she’s always been known is ready for yet another summer at the beach. Each year Belly’s mother packs up Belly and her brother and heads to her best friend’s beach house with Susannah and her two sons, Conrad and Jeremiah, at Cousins Beach.<br /><br />Every year Belly has gotten more and more of a crush on Conrad and every year Belly is the little sister the boys never had. This summer however Belly is starting to blossom and change and really hopes the summer will be different.<br /><br />The Summer I Turned Pretty wasn’t too bad of a read, a bit out of my normal reading spectrum maybe but turned into a decent coming of age tale. Belly is obviously young and naive in the story and in some ways that made it seem a bit unbelievable as kids these days generally are more advanced at her age. This in a way made this one feel a bit dated as if it were something from decades ago, along the lines of Dirty Dancing and Baby being naive and growing over the summer just without the dancing side. Of course I loved that movie so when giving up trying to picture the story in this decade I found myself enjoying it more.<br /><br />For more reviews please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://carriesbookreviews.com/">https://carriesbookreviews.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17844224030136554525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1371160737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1371160737" />
    <a title="Sky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32831460-sky"><img alt="Sky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590554430p2/32831460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1371160737?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sky" href="/user/show/32831460-sky">Sky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32831460-sky?shelf=could-not-finish">could-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1371160737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14889224356676895684"><b>DNF at 30%</b><br/><br/>I’m sorry to anyone who loved this book. I’m glad you loved this book, really! But this is what makes book world, book world; diversity in opinions.<br/><br/>Okay, <i>The summer I turned pretty</i> is about a girl named Belly (I know), who every summer goes to this beach house they share with their mother’s best friend, who by chance has two swoon-worthy boys. <br/><br/>I was not interested, I was not intrigued, I felt literally nothing. By now the characters names are slipping out of my grasp. Belly, our MC, is</span>
  <span id="freeText14889224356676895684" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 30%</b><br /><br />I’m sorry to anyone who loved this book. I’m glad you loved this book, really! But this is what makes book world, book world; diversity in opinions.<br /><br />Okay, <i>The summer I turned pretty</i> is about a girl named Belly (I know), who every summer goes to this beach house they share with their mother’s best friend, who by chance has two swoon-worthy boys. <br /><br />I was not interested, I was not intrigued, I felt literally nothing. By now the characters names are slipping out of my grasp. Belly, our MC, is a whinny <s>kid</s> teenager who does nothing but complain. She complains that her mama didn’t throw a hissy fit after the divorce. She complains that the boys didn’t play with her. Heck, she complains about the fact that the boys need the toilet seat pulled up and she doesn’t, which reminds her that she’s different than them.<br /> <br />First off, I know no mom who will let their 16..? year old daughter share a bathroom with her brother and his 2 GROWN FRIENDS, while she has her own damn private bathroom. This book was… Vague? Nothing remotely interesting happens. I’m guessing a love triangle is on it’s way, but I see no reason for a love triangle. In real life when you have to choose between a guy who’s moody, dark, and oh-so-mysterious, you go for the damn perky brother! The way the author tried to match up their appearances with their personalities got me to tears. I remember when I was 12 I used to read these cheesy romance stories online where the author named her characters Tune, Pride, etc.. because obviously one can sing and the other is prideful..? Well it wasn’t in English so it didn’t sound as bad. I couldn’t help but compare this with it, Conrad with his <i>smirky kind of mouth</i>, and his dark eyes and dark soul and dark BS. And Jeremiah with his messy blonde hair, dishevelled appearance, and perky personality. I just couldn’t not bring myself to laugh. <br /><br />And why is this book so obsessed with appearances? Looking pretty or in Belly’s case; prettier won’t change your entire life. That just shows how shallow these characters are.<br /><i>“You're so pretty. So pretty. You're going to have an amazing, amazing summer. It'll be a summer you'll never forget.”</i> Because that’s all it takes to have the summer of your life!<br /><br />Also, the writing style was just one dimensional, I didn’t feel anything for the characters, I didn’t care for them; no hate nor love. I’m disappointed I didn’t enjoy this as much as many others. Oh well, I hope I like <i>To all the boys I’ve loved before.</i><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14889224356676895684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_317925502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317925502" />
    <a title="Amy (Turn the Page)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5535721-amy-turn-the-page"><img alt="Amy (Turn the Page)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343817781p2/5535721.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317925502?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy (Turn the Page)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy (Turn the Page)" href="/user/show/5535721-amy-turn-the-page">Amy (Turn the Page)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7956260-the-summer-i-turned-pretty">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317925502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15243803302279045956"><i>The Summer I Turned Pretty</i> is the first book in a YA series that by all accounts, seems to be well-loved and incredibly popular.<br/><br/>It’s your typical teenage love-triangle set against a pretty backdrop of sea, sun and sand, and not a whole lot else. With these types of books, when we all know what’s going to happen, it’s the characters and dialogue that really make the story.<br/><br/>It’s a pity then, that I so intensely disliked Isabel.<br/><br/>She was, to put it bluntly, a brat. (Other words I came to associate wit</span>
  <span id="freeText15243803302279045956" style="display:none"><i>The Summer I Turned Pretty</i> is the first book in a YA series that by all accounts, seems to be well-loved and incredibly popular.<br /><br />It’s your typical teenage love-triangle set against a pretty backdrop of sea, sun and sand, and not a whole lot else. With these types of books, when we all know what’s going to happen, it’s the characters and dialogue that really make the story.<br /><br />It’s a pity then, that I so intensely disliked Isabel.<br /><br />She was, to put it bluntly, a brat. (Other words I came to associate with her included, but were not limited to: dull, spoilt, petulant, willfully ignorant, entitled little… madam.)<br /><br />The moment Conrad, the elder boy-next-door is described, it’s so very obvious where this is all going, but it will still take three books to get there. And that’s great… if you enjoy the books. Sadly, I really, really didn’t. Conrad is the brother Isabel (sorry, but I simply refuse to call her Belly) has been <s>obsessed</s> in love with since she was ten. The dark-haired, soulful, guitar-playing one. Great at everything without even trying and who, interestingly, shows no apparent interest in Isabel for most of the book. His younger brother, Jeremiah doesn’t stand a chance really. Needless to say, I actually liked him better, although it’s a shame his character is never really developed beyond the designated lighthearted best friend. Perhaps it’s for the best, Jeremiah, when all’s said and done. I sense some painful times ahead for you.<br /><br />I can totally see why this series is such a hit – what teenage girl doesn’t dream of suddenly morphing into a natural beauty, not to mention having all these hot guys fighting over you? But as an older reader, hearing over and over and over again how Isabel has ‘blossomed’ overnight quickly started to grate. It annoyed me that all anyone has to say about Isabel is related to her good looks. It irritated me that Isabel doesn’t have any hobbies, friends, aspirations, or life outside of the two months she spends at Cousin Beach. I disliked her attitude and her mooning over Conrad. And I absolutely hated how she played one brother of the other.<br /><br />Thankfully and rather refreshingly, Han doesn’t feel the need to give one brother the typical bad-boy persona in this love-triangle. The natural choice would be Conrad, but in reality, he and Isabel barely interact, we just constantly hear about him courtesy of you-know-who. It’s almost painful to read really. Isabel acts as though they are in a romantic relationship when really it’s all in her head. She’s like a possessive, slightly crazy, ex-girlfriend. At one point, Conrad tells her, quite rightly, that there is no way that she, a 15-year-old kid, is leaving a party alone in the car of some strange guy that none of them even know. Isabel, in response, promptly throws a tantrum and literally screams insults at him and the girl he is talking to at the time. Conrad doesn’t treat Isabel badly, he treats her like she is: a whiney kid. Because, sadly, that’s all this girl does. Obsess and sulk.<br /><br />Isabel is, I suppose, a stereotypical portrayal of a teenager. Incredibly young, naive, hormonal and completely self-absorbed. I imagine some readers will feel sorry for her, perhaps relate to how she is feeling, that first major crush, the pains of growing up etc. I couldn’t. I just didn’t like her. Isabel may well grow up a lot in the next two books, but I don’t have the patience or the inclination to watch this girl manipulate these two guys any further, going back and forth between them and probably forever damaging their relationship as brothers in the process. (There was also a <i>third</i> guy, Cam, who was far too nice and intelligent to deserve to be treated the way he was.)<br /><br />The highlight of the book, for me, was the friendship between Susannah and Isabel’s mother. I loved how close they were, the way they confided their hardships and marriage problems in one another, how they would get away from life for a little while every summer to connect with themselves and each other, no men allowed. It was interesting seeing their relationship through Isabel’s eyes and I felt Han captured their bond very well. I just wish the story had focused on this aspect instead of being all about teenage angst.<br /><br />I didn’t hate <i>The Summer I Turned Pretty</i>, but I’d be lying if I said I thought it was good storytelling. It wasn’t until I had finished reading, that it occurred to me just how little there is to this book, and just how much I disliked the main character. Do I recommend it? No. Though I suppose it’s a reasonable enough choice for a summer beach read, if you’re not the kind to be put off by a lack of real plot (which the constant backwards and forwards timeline couldn’t disguise), underdeveloped or underused characters or a worn-out, cliché, set up. But really, why bother, when there are so much more engaging and fun, summer-romance books out there to be read?</span>
  <a data-text-id="15243803302279045956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11669883646412323068">284 pages where absolutely nothing happened.<br/><br/>I originally wanted to give it a star, but well, at least I finished the book, so this is me being nice. I've read many books with annoying-but-bearable protagonists, but this one made me want to pull my own hair out.<br/><br/><b>Edit:</b> I changed my mind, bye.<br/><br/>Belly wasn't <i>that</i> bad, but whenever I tried to like her, she immediately did something entirely stupid and I just had to hate her all over again. Not exaggerating, but she was annoying 90% of the time. Like how</span>
  <span id="freeText11669883646412323068" style="display:none">284 pages where absolutely nothing happened.<br /><br />I originally wanted to give it a star, but well, at least I finished the book, so this is me being nice. I've read many books with annoying-but-bearable protagonists, but this one made me want to pull my own hair out.<br /><br /><b>Edit:</b> I changed my mind, bye.<br /><br />Belly wasn't <i>that</i> bad, but whenever I tried to like her, she immediately did something entirely stupid and I just had to hate her all over again. Not exaggerating, but she was annoying 90% of the time. Like how many boys was she interested in at the same time? Did she even realize she was basically hurting every one of them by making a move on all of them at once? (Probably not on Jeremiah at least, but he was hurt by it too, okay?)<br /><br />Belly was constantly lying to herself about who she actually liked. It was so damn obvious that it had always been Conrad, but what did she do? Flirt with everyone else to make him jealous? Seriously? *roll eyes for the 100th time* Look, I've been avoiding this cliche all my life. Also, can she just stop whining about every single thing that happened? I honestly hate that kind of main characters. PLEASE STOP COMPLAINING AND ENJOY EVEN JUST AN HOUR OF YOUR LIFE.<br />Plus, please stop overreacting at stuff that wasn't even that bad to begin with.<br /><br />My other complaints about this book includes:<br /><i>Boring love interest(s):</i> What kind of romance novel have such <i>boring</i> love interests? I didn't even get to know that much about any of them and the book ENDED. What was the whole plot even about? The whole thing couldn't actually have been <i>only</i> about a very annoying Isabel and her constant complaints of her long-time crush not liking back.... Right?<br />Hell no. And don't even get me started on how many boys there were. 3. I really really dislike love triangles but at least that was endurable. But THIS?! NOooooO. Just no. To make it worse, I absolutely cheered for none of them. Everyone was just completely dull. And (for the third time, maybe) Belly's whiny narration didn't help.<br /><br /><i>Writing Style:</i><br />-Too much dialogue and not enough <i>feels</i> into the story.<br />-Very easy to go through but absolutely no plot at all.<br />-Chapters are too short and are often cut off to skip to another scenes. (It's extremely frustrating.)</span>

    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54835325-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598113126p2/54835325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2519783260?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/54835325-kat">Kat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54835325-kat?shelf=library-2">library-2</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2519783260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6575054165750416376">What a perfect summer beach read! Belly is 15 about to turn 16 and spends every summer at the beach with her mom’s family friend, who has two sons, Jeremiah and Conrad. The complicated relationships there are the focus of the book. Belly has had a crush on older son Conrad since forever, but he’s two years older and mostly sees her as pretty annoying. And in all fairness, Belly is definitely the least mature of the group, but then she’s also the youngest. Can we blame a guy going into college in</span>
  <span id="freeText6575054165750416376" style="display:none">What a perfect summer beach read! Belly is 15 about to turn 16 and spends every summer at the beach with her mom’s family friend, who has two sons, Jeremiah and Conrad. The complicated relationships there are the focus of the book. Belly has had a crush on older son Conrad since forever, but he’s two years older and mostly sees her as pretty annoying. And in all fairness, Belly is definitely the least mature of the group, but then she’s also the youngest. Can we blame a guy going into college in the fall for not being interested in a 15-year-old? I could see Jenny Han turning Belly into an awesome character like Lara Jean as she grows up and matures. She’s only 15. And I loved the family relationships in this one. Jenny Han always does a great job with those. Susannah was one of my favorite characters! Excited to read book two. 5/5 Beachy sandy stars.<br /><br />Please excuse typos/name misspellings. Entered on screen reader.<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1673327306" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=average">average</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=cute-and-or-easy-reads">cute-and-or-easy-reads</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1673327306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer188359049772039571"><i>The Summer I Turned Pretty</i> is the definition of a “typical” summer-on-the-beach read. It’s cute. It’s easy to read. It’s romantic and fun. It's an overall enjoyable read, even if it wasn’t unique in the slightest.<br/><br/>Besides the story and characters not feeling unique, I really couldn’t stand the name Belly. I know it’s supposed to be a nickname from Isabel — but <i>why</i> Belly? Again, I know it's explained in the story — I’m asking this more towards the author. I think Isabel is a pretty name. Why not B</span>
  <span id="freeText188359049772039571" style="display:none"><i>The Summer I Turned Pretty</i> is the definition of a “typical” summer-on-the-beach read. It’s cute. It’s easy to read. It’s romantic and fun. It's an overall enjoyable read, even if it wasn’t unique in the slightest.<br /><br />Besides the story and characters not feeling unique, I really couldn’t stand the name Belly. I know it’s supposed to be a nickname from Isabel — but <i>why</i> Belly? Again, I know it's explained in the story — I’m asking this more towards the author. I think Isabel is a pretty name. Why not Belle, instead?<br /><br />This story has romance, humor, sadness, conflict … but all at a light level. Nothing is heavy, which is to be expected from an easy summer read. If anything, I wish we would have gotten more of Conrad and Belly. I realize this is a series and their friendship/relationship will continue to progress throughout the series, but I don’t know if I want to buy the rest of the series. At least, not now. I wasn’t too impressed.<br /><br />I read Han’s <i>To All the Boys I’ve Loved Before</i> and adored that series. It was a blast to read during my travels in Europe. That series was the reason I bought this novel. However, this series just doesn’t feel the same. It doesn’t even feel like it was written by Han. Either way, I’ll probably finish this series down the road (or later this summer break). Then again, I might not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="188359049772039571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15864334318223449645" style="display:none"><b> 2.5-3 stars </b><br><br>A very cute beach read. I only read this because I loved Han's TATBILB series and wanted to read more by her. This book is VERY different from her others.     <a title="Shaikha Alahmad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55334362-shaikha-alahmad"><img alt="Shaikha Alahmad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583758717p2/55334362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1748083359?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaikha Alahmad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaikha Alahmad" href="/user/show/55334362-shaikha-alahmad">Shaikha Alahmad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7956260-the-summer-i-turned-pretty">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1748083359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1741990298432342668"><b>
  <i>"I think he would have stayed with <i>her</i> forever, trying to figure out the mystery. He was a puzzle solver, the kind of person who likes theorems, theories. X always had to equal something. It couldn't just be X".</i>
</b><br/><br/>Isabel "<i>Belly</i>" measures her life in summers, it has always been the most important time of the year. Everything good, everything magical and everything special happens between the months of June and August. It's when her family shares a beach house with her mother's best friend, Susan</span>
  <span id="freeText1741990298432342668" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"I think he would have stayed with <i>her</i> forever, trying to figure out the mystery. He was a puzzle solver, the kind of person who likes theorems, theories. X always had to equal something. It couldn't just be X".</i>
</b><br /><br />Isabel "<i>Belly</i>" measures her life in summers, it has always been the most important time of the year. Everything good, everything magical and everything special happens between the months of June and August. It's when her family shares a beach house with her mother's best friend, Susannah, and her two sons. Like Belly's older brother, Steven, Susannah's boys have always thought of Belly as their younger sister. Jeremiah and Conrad; they are the boys that Belly has known since her very first summer - they have been her brother figures, her crushes, and everything in between. But one summer, one wonderful and terrible summer, everything changes.<br /><br />A beautiful book that hit me <u>right in the feels</u>.<br />I couldn't decide whether to give this 4 or 5 stars, so I'm settling for <b>4.5/5</b><br />As usual, I cried like a baby and I absolutely cannot wait to read the second book. 😩📚<br /><br />Oh and guys, I have a crush on Conrad... 👅</span>
  <a data-text-id="1741990298432342668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those that have always wished for the perfect summer, for that perfect someone.</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156773656" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1205092946062901528">Rating: 4.5<br/><br/>I'm so glad I bought this with me now. It's one of those books that guarantee's you butterflies and giggles.<br/><br/>Every summer Belly visits cousins Beach with her mother and brother. There they meet up with Susannah (her mothers best friend) and her two boy's, Conrad and Jeremiah. Belly has always loved Conrad. But she has always been able to rely on Jer. He's the safety net, the sweet, uncomplicated best friend type-of-guy. But this summer promises to be different. You see, Belly's all gro</span>
  <span id="freeText1205092946062901528" style="display:none">Rating: 4.5<br /><br />I'm so glad I bought this with me now. It's one of those books that guarantee's you butterflies and giggles.<br /><br />Every summer Belly visits cousins Beach with her mother and brother. There they meet up with Susannah (her mothers best friend) and her two boy's, Conrad and Jeremiah. Belly has always loved Conrad. But she has always been able to rely on Jer. He's the safety net, the sweet, uncomplicated best friend type-of-guy. But this summer promises to be different. You see, Belly's all grown up and both boys can no longer ignore the obvious. Belly's turning into a woman, a pretty woman.<br /><br />What I love most are those spine tingling moments. Where my own reaction matches Belly's so closely. It's kind of hard not to be mad at her when she does dumb things, to not fall in love with Conrad when he gives you that sly grin, and feel sorry for poor Jeremiah. To not want to hold Susannah.<br /><br />Reading it a second time did bring a few things to my attention. For one, I'm not too sure if I like Belly's mum all that much. And I'm not okay with Susannah not talking her boys through the divorce. To just leaving them in the dark.<br /><br />I fell in love with this book all over again in those short few hours. But a lot of the time I tried to hold back frustration when it came to knowing how much of a mess the last book would be. I tried to ignore that part. To focus on what I was reading at that very moment. It's easier said then done.<br /><br />So it's not all that deep. But dammit I can't forget how it made me feel the first time I read it. Hardcore butterflies. A book hasn't made me feel like that in a long time. And even now when I read a line or two involving Conrad being his usual cool self. Dude, I swoon.<br /></span>
